                            '\n'
                            '```turtle\n'
                            '@prefix foaf: <http://xmlns.com/foaf/0.1/>.\n'
                            '\n'
                            '<#person1> a foaf:Person; foaf:name "Person1"; '
                            'foaf:knows <#person2>, <#person3>.\n'

                            'foaf:knows <#person2>, ..., <#person49>.\n'
                            '```\n'
                            '\n'
                            'This is a relatively straightforward structure, '
                            'and the idea is to have each person know at least '
                            'two other people. For instance, Person1 knows '
                            'Person2 and Person3. These people then know other '
                            'people, and so on. The "foaf:knows" data property '
                            'is used to establish these relationships. This '
                            'data is then naturally scalable to the amount of '
                            'people you need.\n'
                            '\n'
                            'Foaf is an ontology used to describe relations '
                            "between people. Each 'person' is given a unique "
                            'identifier, which is used to link data. '
                            "'Foaf:knows' is a commonly used relation in this "
                            'ontology, which can be used to describe the '
                            'social network of each person.\n'
                            '\n'
                            "Note: As this platform can't showcase 50 persons, "
                            'this is a brief example. However, when generating '
                            'such a dataset, unique connections between the '
                            'individuals are needed to avoid a hierarchy-like '
                            'structure. Also, a validation is needed to '
                            'prevent any kind of looping (person1 knowing '
                            'person2, person2 knowing person1) as well as to '
                            'check that each person knows at least 2 and at '
                            'most 49 other persons. As the turtle format can '
                            'become unwieldy and chaotic with these many '
                            'connections, careful planning and organization '
                            'are required. Then, separate each person’s links '
                            'to others to prevent confusion.')])
